              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2459470-lisa-kay?shelf=reviewed-by-me">reviewed-by-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2459470-lisa-kay?shelf=season-winter">season-winter</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2459470-lisa-kay?shelf=authors-e">authors-e</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2459470-lisa-kay?shelf=authors-h">authors-h</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer182626878" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8793906879798956310"><i>The <b>primrose</b>, usually the first flower of spring (from the Latin “prima”), represents <i><b>enduring love</b></i>. In the Language of Flowers, it means “I can't live without you.” It tells your significant other, “I am yours forever.”</i><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379764601i/229498.jpg' width='65' height='85' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380352716i/706133.jpg' width='85' height='85' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380352716i/706134._SX540_.jpg' width='80' height='85' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380352716i/706135._SX540_.jpg' width='100' height='85' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380352716i/706136.gif' width='55' height='85' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379764601i/229500._SX540_.jpg' width='80' height='85' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>★★★★½ The world-building in this epic romantic-time-travel-fantasy is superior, the characters wonderful. Some people find Rhapsody, the heroine, to be too much of a “Mary Sue” – if that is even possible for someone with her back ground! I found her delightful and felt her losses</span>
  <span id="freeText8793906879798956310" style="display:none"><i>The <b>primrose</b>, usually the first flower of spring (from the Latin “prima”), represents <i><b>enduring love</b></i>. In the Language of Flowers, it means “I can't live without you.” It tells your significant other, “I am yours forever.”</i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379764601i/229498.jpg" width="65" height="85" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380352716i/706133.jpg" width="85" height="85" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380352716i/706134._SX540_.jpg" width="80" height="85" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380352716i/706135._SX540_.jpg" width="100" height="85" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380352716i/706136.gif" width="55" height="85" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379764601i/229500._SX540_.jpg" width="80" height="85" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>★★★★½ The world-building in this epic romantic-time-travel-fantasy is superior, the characters wonderful. Some people find Rhapsody, the heroine, to be too much of a “Mary Sue” – if that is even possible for someone with her back ground! I found her delightful and felt her losses. **shrugs** Go figure.<br><br>This book is spell-binding, the characters anything but cardboard cutout figurines – so often found in other books – and the mystery entertaining. The developing camaraderie between the three main protagonists is entertaining and truly the “guts” of this first in the <i>Symphony of Ages</i> series. I almost gave up on their endless journey along the Root, but it was so worth it when they finally hit the light of day. I’m guessing the heart – or romance – comes in the second book; one I’m looking forward to! Plus, I’m hearing rumors of seventh book, <i>The Merchant Emperor</i> in Spring, 2012. Yippee!<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/261604.Rhapsody_Child_of_Blood__Symphony_of_Ages___1_" title="Rhapsody Child of Blood (Symphony of Ages, #1) by Elizabeth Haydon" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/books/1312053846s/261604.jpg" alt="Rhapsody Child of Blood (Symphony of Ages, #1) by Elizabeth Haydon" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/515587.Prophecy_Child_of_Earth__Symphony_of_Ages___2_" title="Prophecy Child of Earth (Symphony of Ages, #2) by Elizabeth Haydon" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/books/1312057499s/515587.jpg" alt="Prophecy Child of Earth (Symphony of Ages, #2) by Elizabeth Haydon" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4490376-sarah-mac?shelf=drank-the-haterade">drank-the-haterade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4490376-sarah-mac?shelf=uber-disappointing">uber-disappointing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4490376-sarah-mac?shelf=sheep-tsunami">sheep-tsunami</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4490376-sarah-mac?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4490376-sarah-mac?shelf=mary-sue-puke-bucket">mary-sue-puke-bucket</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4490376-sarah-mac?shelf=zzz-2018-chunkster-hell">zzz-2018-chunkster-hell</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4490376-sarah-mac?shelf=zzz-2018">zzz-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1007627199" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16928509180048196271">DNF, some point after the Fire Incident...pg 220 or so? Whatever. <br/><br/>There comes a time with mediocre doorstoppers when you put the book down, stare at the wall, check the page count yet again, & say: "I don't give a rat's ass about this. So why am I still reading?" <br/><br/>Friends, I've reached that point with RHAPSODY. <br/><br/>There's just too much waffling tedium (ffs, it takes for-fucking-ever to get out of the stupid root system) to excite my curiosity & push forward. It's the worst kind of epic fantasy -- th</span>
  <span id="freeText16928509180048196271" style="display:none">DNF, some point after the Fire Incident...pg 220 or so? Whatever. <br /><br />There comes a time with mediocre doorstoppers when you put the book down, stare at the wall, check the page count yet again, &amp; say: "I don't give a rat's ass about this. So why am I still reading?" <br /><br />Friends, I've reached that point with RHAPSODY. <br /><br />There's just too much waffling tedium (ffs, it takes for-fucking-ever to get out of the stupid root system) to excite my curiosity &amp; push forward. It's the worst kind of epic fantasy -- that is, endless wandering around a pseudo-medieval world with vague menaces pursuing the protags as they reluctantly band together &amp; learn trust. Zzzzzz. Combine that with Rhapsody's gag-inducing Mary Sue Disease (forget sugary-sweet Anne of THE INNOCENT -- Rhapsody makes her look like Bellatrix LeStrange) &amp; a tedious Tolkien remix of villainy (the tower? the eye? puh-lease), &amp; it's a hearty good night. <br /><br />As I've said in other reviews, I don't necessarily mind Tolkien homage in one's epic fantasy (example: GREEN RIDER), but the book still needs to differentiate itself somehow. It needs to have characters that compel completion. It needs to be, y'know, <i>good.</i> Here? There's no dimension to the characters; the world building is a muddle; the plot begins in the middle &amp; rarely offers explanations enough to orient the reader; heroes &amp; villains are totally black &amp; white (excepting, perhaps, Grunthor &amp; Achmed, but I don't care enough to wade through for their sake); the baddies are lolzy in their obvious "Hate me! Booo, hiss!!" (Michael enjoys torture, manipulation, murder, rape, AND child molesting -- overkill, much?); the overall plot is meandering &amp; unfocused; the time travel aspect bores me...<br /><br />And so, farewell to RHAPSODY. By the time I'd asked myself why I was still reading, my brain had already checked out, run to the library, &amp; stopped for Starbucks -- because caffeine &amp; better books are the cure for everything.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16928509180048196271" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11183129267436421236">Rating 2.0 stars - DNF<br/><br/> This book seemed like a bait and switch. When I read the synopsis it described a story about a woman named Rhapsody who got kidnapped. I listened to the audiobook for 2 hours and there was no Rhapsody! I looked a few times to see if I had the wrong book.   <span id="freeText11183129267436421236" style="display:none">Rating 2.0 stars - DNF<br /><br /> This book seemed like a bait and switch. When I read the synopsis it described a story about a woman named Rhapsody who got kidnapped. I listened to the audiobook for 2 hours and there was no Rhapsody! I looked a few times to see if I had the wrong book. Then I decided to go and read some reviews and found out the characters that I had listened about for those 2 hours, I wouldn't find out what happened to them until the last few chapters of the book. The book is 30 hours long though. I don't have that much patience. I read some reviews that mentioned how it got better and that I just needed to hang in there, but I just can't do it. I feel like the author tricked me into reading about something else entirely and even IF she delivered on her promised story in the rest of the book, at this point I feel cheated and don't want to finish. </span>

<div id="review_226060317" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/226060317" />
    <a title="Chris Cutler" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2652771-chris-cutler"><img alt="Chris Cutler" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415936269p2/2652771.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/226060317?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris Cutler" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris Cutler" href="/user/show/2652771-chris-cutler">Chris Cutler</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Chris by: </span>
      Christy
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer226060317" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9484076815863241714">Someone spilled a very good story across 650 pages and left several dozen really incredible pieces soaking in puddles of soggy text. I agree with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/20586951' rel='nofollow noopener'>the reviewer who said</a> Rhapsody is "a romance novel heroine, thrown into a fantasy novel." As much as my other complaints, the oft annoying and ever self-righteous heroine lost this book its third star.<br/><br/>I wish I had been able to like this book, because some of the ideas are truly great. Haydon's version of Naming magic and Time-slipping are appealing and</span>
  <span id="freeText9484076815863241714" style="display:none">Someone spilled a very good story across 650 pages and left several dozen really incredible pieces soaking in puddles of soggy text. I agree with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/20586951" rel="nofollow noopener">the reviewer who said</a> Rhapsody is "a romance novel heroine, thrown into a fantasy novel." As much as my other complaints, the oft annoying and ever self-righteous heroine lost this book its third star.<br /><br />I wish I had been able to like this book, because some of the ideas are truly great. Haydon's version of Naming magic and Time-slipping are appealing and original adaptations of these genre staples. The Brother's blood-lore and Achmed's path-lore are ingenious and intriguing magics in themselves, and the transition from one to the other as the book progresses is laudable. I also liked the world that was built, in which elf- and orc-analogs are accompanied by a handful of other races, each with their own characteristics.<br /><br />My very favorite part of the book is a beautiful metaphor of leaving doors open in a house, finally allowing Rhapsody to reach closure in her grieving. This is followed by the masterful and humorous chapter told through the eyes of a fire priest. In fact, Haydon's writing is best when it changes to 3rd person limited, a technique she should have use much more heavily (or exclusively) instead of the omniscient POV she usually adopts.<br /><br />Unfortunately, there are three major problems. The most noticeable of these is redundancy. Not only is there a reminder on each page that Rhapsody is the most beautiful woman in creation, but every other element of the story and mythos are repeated at least three times just to make sure that the reader caught it and knows how things will work out.<br /><br />The worst problem is (frequent) inconsistency. POV characters know (and later forget?) things they shouldn't. Magical abilities aren't used in situations when they should be. In one breath the characters speak with pride of their racial (non-human) heritage, yet in the next speak of non-humans as the outsiders. Passing time allows for the rise and fall of nations, but not for people to change or learn anything besides swordplay. Rhapsody's mood swings are often as incomprehensible as they are counterproductive to her development as a character.<br /><br />The third problem, and the one that really gives the sense of having been spilled, is the way Hayden throws away lines or chapters chock-full of potential. The worst instance for me was when the above-mentioned doors metaphor had absolutely no bearing on Rhapsody as a character. We were promised a turning point, but this went unfulfilled. Throughout the book there are so many sentences crafted to hold meaning, but the story just admires the flowery words and moves on. Rarely is a skillful phrase actually used to do something other than ornament the page. And there is so much perfume added to the text that the actually pleasant scents get lost in a sticky muddle.<br /><br />From reading the synopses for the next several books, it is clear that the imminent threat is always "unimaginable devastation" or "war unlike any the world has ever seen." I'm already bored. Please just make me care about the people.<br /><br />All of that is a long way of saying that no, I won't be continuing this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9484076815863241714" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('dLdCbKVtl1ibe/XOtutAxcl/k12qZ+U20zi6XcRNMUbd0TZpXB8CU5L4hFx6yAeBUCxANSdPEEikBR3P5UCgrw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('DHvrFNhJ1bSXuYeKB2ONGlWcQ3V+8BgRsNAvU4SgfxGlHZ8RITtAv5469hjLQMpezM+QHfPY7W/H7YjBpa3u+A==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer17961919389588900359">Elizabeth Haydon (* 1965 in Michigan) is a fantasy author, whose 1999 debut, Rhapsody: Child of Blood, garnered comparisons with Goodkind, Jordan, and even Tolkien. She has written two fantasy series set within the same universe, The fantasy/romance/whodunit fusion called The Symphony of Ages and the young adult series The Lost Journals of Ven Polypheme.<br/><br/>An herbalist, harpist, and madrigal singer, </span>
  <span id="freeText17961919389588900359" style="display:none">Elizabeth Haydon (* 1965 in Michigan) is a fantasy author, whose 1999 debut, Rhapsody: Child of Blood, garnered comparisons with Goodkind, Jordan, and even Tolkien. She has written two fantasy series set within the same universe, The fantasy/romance/whodunit fusion called The Symphony of Ages and the young adult series The Lost Journals of Ven Polypheme.<br /><br />An herbalist, harpist, and madrigal singer, Elizabeth Haydon also enjoys anthropology and folklore. She lives on the East Coast of the United States.<br /><br />For more information, please see <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elizabeth_Haydon">http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elizabet...</a></span>
